  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b641f4bc-cd91-406d-8594-a474397e81a0'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/82348831-hazel"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1527880899i/82348831._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/82348831-hazel">Hazel</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">You cannot read books on Goodreads. The website is simply for rating books and getting book recommendations. The Read button is in the past tense, as <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">You cannot read books on Goodreads. The website is simply for rating books and getting book recommendations. The Read button is in the past tense, as in you have read the book. By clicking that button, you are saying that you have read the book already. In order to actually read a book, you need to check it out at the library or purchase it.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

  <span id="freeText7387656879444608344" style="display:none">Why Scourge hates Tigerstar...<br />Tiny goes to the forest, running away when Ruby and Socks say that his owners will throw him in the river.<br />When he crosses Thunderclan territory, he meets a patrol with Bluestar, Thistleclaw, and Tigerpaw (Tigerstar).<br />Thistleclaw tells Tigerpaw to attack Tiny, while Bluestar is telling them that Tiny is no threat to Thunderclan. Tigerpaw attacks and nearly kills Tiny, but Bluestar tells Tigerpaw that he taught Tiny a lesson. Scourge is out for revenge...<br /><br />Scourge wouldn't be evil by now if...<br /><br />Ok first of all, quit saying it is Tigerpaw's fault for Scourge being evil! THISTLECLAW gave him the order, as his MENTOR. THISTLECLAW taught Tigerpaw how to be evil, murderous, and his hunger power.<br />ALSO... it's actually NOT Thistleclaw's fault either!<br />It all started in Crookedstar's promise. When Crookedjaw is dreaming in the dark forest, he is being trained by Mapleshade. Meanwhile, Thistleclaw is in the same place training the deathbite with Shredtail and Mapleshade asks Crookedjaw if he wanted to learn it. <br /><br />It is mainly SHREDTAIL'S fault. If Thistleclaw wasn't mentored by him, he wouldn't be evil, he wouldn't have mentored Tigerpaw to be cruel, and Tigerpaw wouldn't attack Scourge. So it's ALL thanks to SHREDTAIL.<br />Also, Bluestar wouldn't have gave her kits away,(Mistystar, Stonefur, and Mosskit),and Mosskit wouldn't have frozen to death when Bluestar was sending her kits to Riverclan. <br /><br />So this is the truth on why Scourge is evil. Pretty sad, huh? </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer726701637660282055">By far the superior of the Graystripe graphic novels. "The Rise of Scourge" has a great story and really good drawing. (I refuse to admit that this is manga, but this art is much more befitting of a book called manga.) I love the art. I don't like to buy these books because they're so short--this one only has 79 pages of actual story--but I liked this one enough that I might have to get it for myself. <br/>I was very impressed with this book. Scourge is one of my favorite characters from Warriors, so</span>
  <span id="freeText726701637660282055" style="display:none">By far the superior of the Graystripe graphic novels. "The Rise of Scourge" has a great story and really good drawing. (I refuse to admit that this is manga, but this art is much more befitting of a book called manga.) I love the art. I don't like to buy these books because they're so short--this one only has 79 pages of actual story--but I liked this one enough that I might have to get it for myself. <br />I was very impressed with this book. Scourge is one of my favorite characters from Warriors, so reading this is really interesting. It makes so much of The Darkest Hour just click.<br />Pros: great art, story, etc.<br />Cons: so short :( And there isn't a sequel. Waah! Poor book just lost a star.<br />Hopes and Dreams: More character singles such as this will be drawn/written, e.g. Yellowfang, Tigerstar, Spottedleaf.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer350432175" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1745188086724090397"> Scourge was born as "Tiny", one of three in a litter. His littermates, Socks and Ruby, did not like him at all. The only time they would even play with him was when "Mama" made them. Ruby even told Tiny that he would be thrown in the river, since no twolegs wanted him as a pet. <br/> So, Tiny ran off to live on the streets. He shed the name "Tiny" and everything about his old life, and quickly becomes the head of the street cats.<br/> When his littermates come crawling to him for help after being left be</span>
  <span id="freeText1745188086724090397" style="display:none"> Scourge was born as "Tiny", one of three in a litter. His littermates, Socks and Ruby, did not like him at all. The only time they would even play with him was when "Mama" made them. Ruby even told Tiny that he would be thrown in the river, since no twolegs wanted him as a pet. <br /> So, Tiny ran off to live on the streets. He shed the name "Tiny" and everything about his old life, and quickly becomes the head of the street cats.<br /> When his littermates come crawling to him for help after being left behind when their twolegs moved, he allows them to eat, then shuns them from his area forever. <br /> His sister, Ruby, made a comment about him being out for blood, and he replies that that is his way of life and that she is too weak. This is how he comes to name his clan, BloodClan.<br /> In the end, he settles his differences with ThunderClan by killing their leader, and then brags about how much he has changed.</span>

  <span id="freeText12269915591270871643" style="display:none">This was a good story, but I wish it had been in writing book form, not manga- I feel like the story was rushed, and it could have been described much better in a regular book way, not a graphic novel type thing. But still, the story had a strange affect on me. <br /><br />When I read Warriors: The Darkest Hour, I hated Scourge. He was a cruel, ruthless villain, killing all those cats and all those other things that he did. I was glad when he died. But now...now I can't help seeing the tiny little cute kitten he once was. I felt so sorry for him at the beginning of this book, and I can understand why he grew cold and evil! I sympathize with him, and I don't think he is entirely bad...I actually like him now. I am sad that he died, if you can believe it- because he could have changed back to what he once was. </span>

Scourge was in the normal Warriors book series and this manga is all about his history.   <span id="freeText17662541064040131733" style="display:none"> This Warriors manga is probably my favorite one in the manga series. I'm not kidding but I literally read the ENTIRE book in one day because I just couldn't put it down. (No, it doesn't have more than 10 pages, it's a manga, people. There's like, 72 pages). Scourge was in the normal Warriors book series and this manga is all about his history. (SPOILER COMING UP, WARNING) The book is his amazing history all the way down to when he passed away to the Dark Forest. In my opinion, he doesn't deserve it. (The spoiler is over now) You have to read at least the first generation of Warriors to read this manga to really understand everything. In my opinion, Scourge in my favorite character in not only the manga, but the entire Warriors world of books itself. The mangas, guides, series, everything. Not only is his history pretty interesting but as a character he's just awesome :D I suggest this and other Warriors manga (mainly this one) to all Warriors fans.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12519569955516291980"> Prologue<br/><br/>I let out squeaks of pain as I lay down. I looked uo at Jake, the ginger tom standing over me, my one true love. He looked urgently down at me. I turned my attention on my swollen belly. I took many deep breaths. The female house folk who gives me food stayed up late into the night to watch.   <span id="freeText12519569955516291980" style="display:none"> Prologue<br /><br />I let out squeaks of pain as I lay down. I looked uo at Jake, the ginger tom standing over me, my one true love. He looked urgently down at me. I turned my attention on my swollen belly. I took many deep breaths. The female house folk who gives me food stayed up late into the night to watch. The twoleg kits where asleep. There was no question to m or anyone here on what was happening. I was giving birth to my kits.<br />Jake looked puzzled down at me. I couldn't help but be scarred on what was going to happen to me. Everything hurt from the tips of my tail and my claws. I should be able to take care of myself, but I was too weak. I felt so weak that it seemd that I was meaningless. I just wanted this to be over.<br />Then I saw Jake's eye's twinkle. There was a small lump of fur behind me. I looked at my child. The kit had black and white fur and was slowly breathing. Jake began to lick the kit.<br />"It's a boy." He purred. I sighed. There was one out, but it still wasn't over. A few minutes later I saw a new shape come. It was a gray she-kit. Since the black and white kit was already warm, Jake began to lick the girl. I purred. She looked just like me. All of a sudden I felt another piece of fur drop behind me. I turned my head and tilted my head at the kit. It was black and had some white on his front left paw.<br />I starred in discuss at him. He was small, too small. I pushed him aside Jake looked up in horror as he saw me push the kit aside and lie back down.<br />"What did you do that for?" He asked. I looked up into Jake'd green eyes.<br />"Just look at him!" I said.<br />Jake turned his head to look at the small bundle of black fur on the ground. His small eyes where closed and facing back at us. <br />"I don's see anything wrong whit him." He respond. <br />"How coul you not see it?" I asked. Jake ignored me and reached out to warm the black kit too. I hissed at him. <br />"Put him back! Dont't waste any time on...that."<br />"Quince, this kit is a living cat and i'm not going to push him aside because he is small." I gladed up at him.<br />"He won't last two hours!" I said "Don't even bother or you might risk killing our daughter too."<br />Jake looked back at me.<br />"I don't belive this! You're giving up on a cat; you're giving up on a kit, and for what? Just because he seems too small at the first glance?"<br />I couldn't belive this ether;Jake was always wasting his time on meaningless things.<br />"Hes is going to sie!" I hissed.<br />"What if he doesn't? What if we kill him when he was going to live anyway?" He asked "What kind of label would that give us? Murders? Savages? It doesn't matter. We just will know we did the wrong thing."<br />My ears dropped as I realized what I had just said. Jake was right, this wasn't a good idea.<br />"Besides, he could grow up to become a fine cat to good fot others. You just never know." I closed my eyes<br />"Your right, I'm sorry I'm just kind of grouchy after the birth." I said looking at my paws.<br />"I understand." Jake said. He laid his head on my gray fur and I purred. I don't know what it was but everything made sense around him.<br />"He is still small though." I said. Jake opened his eyes.<br />"Well... he can't really help can he?" He asked.<br />"No, I guess not."<br />After I licked the small black kitten severald times, we settled down. The twoleg went to sleep and the three kits all lais beside me. They where so beautiful, well almost all of them. I guess I was being picky and wanting my kits look perfect. Silly me. I really do wish the last one was...normal sized. Was that wrong? It seemed wrong to me.<br />I sighed. He really was a cute kit; maybe I should give him a chance. After all, he is my son. I should be happy that I have a son, but he was small. I guess I have the other two kits. I love the. They didn't have anything wrong with them.<br />"What should we name the kits?" Jake asked.<br />"You can name the black and white kit." I said. Jake looked down at the kit. Names flooded through his head.<br />"Socks." He finally said. I smiled. Socks was a good name. "You should name our daughter. After all, she has her mother's looks."<br />I blushed at his coment and looked down at my daughter. I was lost at names. She looked like me, so maybe I should give her the name I always wanted.<br />"Ruby" I said. "The name fits he perfectly. She will be our little princess." Jake smiled<br />"Socks and Ruby. I like those names." He said "What about this one?" I hade almost forgot about the small black kit in my paws. I didn't want to sound mean so I just responded to Jake.<br />"You can name him." I said.<br />"No, you sould name him." He said. I wondered if he was thinking the same thing I was. Thia kit was so small, so puny, and do tiny, that I hade to make him remember that. I couldn't see any other thing to call him.<br />"He should be named Tiny." Jake looked up at me. "It's the only name will ever fit him."<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12519569955516291980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8262742774909905685">Rating: 6 out of 10<br/><br/>Villains' origins are always very fun to read! This one was fast-paced, engaging, and exciting. I never actually cared about Scourge as a character before, but the manga format sounded interesting enough to check it out.<br/><br/>Even though the story felt rushed at times due to the page length, the way it portrayed Scourge's emotions was impressive for a comic. Since it's a backstory, we already know some of the information given, but I was still surprised by the details. It wasn't as </span>
  <span id="freeText8262742774909905685" style="display:none">Rating: 6 out of 10<br /><br />Villains' origins are always very fun to read! This one was fast-paced, engaging, and exciting. I never actually cared about Scourge as a character before, but the manga format sounded interesting enough to check it out.<br /><br />Even though the story felt rushed at times due to the page length, the way it portrayed Scourge's emotions was impressive for a comic. Since it's a backstory, we already know some of the information given, but I was still surprised by the details. It wasn't as original as it could've been, but it had somewhat of a classic villain vibe to it I really enjoyed, especially considering this is one of the "old" Warriors books.<br /><br />The art wasn't my favorite (I still prefer the newest artist), but the character's expressions worked well and the style looked more similar to a real japanese manga than the current one. <br /><br />Personally, I think the story could have been told better if this was a novella, but the manga format was an original way to show it and I still had a great time reading it! It's very short (it took me only around half an hour to finish it, and I tend to read comics more slowly than the average person) and wildly entertaining so I encourage every Warriors fan to give it a try!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8262742774909905685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_166587022" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166587022" />
    <a title="Jack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5400547-jack"><img alt="Jack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536008080p2/5400547.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166587022?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack" href="/user/show/5400547-jack">Jack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166587022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer276977915627414843">I've just re-read this as I want to re-read the Warriors mangas I have as they're quick, enjoyable reads that I haven't picked up for a while.<br/><br/>So...<br/><br/>Characters - 5/5 - Amazing characters; loved seeing them as images how the manga artist portrayed them. I loved the development of the main cat, Tiny, and how he eventually changed over time into Scourge. The cats also made me smile at the beginning; they were really cute kits arguing like kits would. And then their mother was telling them off, making</span>
  <span id="freeText276977915627414843" style="display:none">I've just re-read this as I want to re-read the Warriors mangas I have as they're quick, enjoyable reads that I haven't picked up for a while.<br /><br />So...<br /><br />Characters - 5/5 - Amazing characters; loved seeing them as images how the manga artist portrayed them. I loved the development of the main cat, Tiny, and how he eventually changed over time into Scourge. The cats also made me smile at the beginning; they were really cute kits arguing like kits would. And then their mother was telling them off, making the characters so believable! Tigerstar also stood out for me with his evilness. <br /><br />Plot - 4/5 - Very good to see such a change in the character of Scourge. The plot was certainly very interesting and exciting throughout. It moved very fast which I loved, though could have possibly expanded at times (we didn't see loads of detail into everything). I would have also liked to have seen a bit more into the detail as to what happened after. It was quite an open ending and I know Scourge did a lot more in his life. <br /><br />Drawing - 4/5 - Pretty good, though I wasn't sure about the look of Tigerstar. He didn't look properly like a cat at all times. I know he's meant to look like a tiger which is another form of cat, but I wasn't too keen. I've also seen better manga's in the past, but most of it was great to look at and read!<br /><br />Enjoyment - 4.5/5 - Lovely, quick read. Maybe TOO quick. I read it in about 15-20 minutes, though quick reads are sort of nice. I also want to see more into Scourge's life, so my rating for this reflects that.<br /><br />Overall - 4.4/5 - A great read that I'd recommend. Not up to the standard of some other mangas out there like Bleach, but it's a lovely compliment to the books. I'll always prefer Erin Hunter for the writing which I think is superb, though the manga artist Dan Jolley did a good job. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="276977915627414843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText15282040059174577446" style="display:none">The Rise of Scourge (Warrior Cats Extra) Summary: When kittypet Tiny crosses paths with some wild forest cats defending their territory, he is left with scars - and a bitter, deep-seated grudge. As his reputation grows among the strays and loners that live in the dirty brick alleyways of Twolegplace, he changes his name to Scourge and puts everything about his old life behind him - except his deadly desire for revenge.<br /><br />MY OPINION<br /><br />Scourge wasn't always an evil cat. Once, eh was just an innocent young kit who was much smaller than his littermates who didn't like him. When an adventure into the woods goes wrong, Tiny, as Scourge was then called, begins to feel a deep resentment toward forest cats - especially Tigerpaw, who attacked him. As Tiny changes his name to Scourge, his power grows and he becomes even more bloodthirsty. When revenge against the forest cats presents itself, Scourge becomes the greatest evil the Clan cats have ever seen.<br /><br />Quote: "The housefolk cub wants us. Not you.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2986812881" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2986812881" />
    <a title="Historyprincess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12881308-historyprincess"><img alt="Historyprincess" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2986812881?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Historyprincess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Historyprincess" href="/user/show/12881308-historyprincess">Historyprincess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/27781574-warriors-volume-4">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12881308-historyprincess?shelf=warriors">warriors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2986812881&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2986812881" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16460599014948483170">Premise: Is it better to be feared than loved if you can't be both? That's the question Tiny has been forced to ask his whole life. Born a kittypet and the runt of his litter, Tiny was constantly – and scornfully – reminded of his size and perceived frailty. But one day, a violent confrontation pushes the kit over the edge, and he strikes out on his own. He quickly learns the ropes of his new life. And it's through this that he grows from a pitiful and bullied kit to a bloodthirsty and vengeful </span>
  <span id="freeText16460599014948483170" style="display:none">Premise: Is it better to be feared than loved if you can't be both? That's the question Tiny has been forced to ask his whole life. Born a kittypet and the runt of his litter, Tiny was constantly – and scornfully – reminded of his size and perceived frailty. But one day, a violent confrontation pushes the kit over the edge, and he strikes out on his own. He quickly learns the ropes of his new life. And it's through this that he grows from a pitiful and bullied kit to a bloodthirsty and vengeful cat with a new name to match his reputation: Scourge.<br /><br />Story/Writing: First off, I will admit this is surprisingly a short read. I read it in just under an hour. I did kind of expect more, but I was satisfied with what I got. I remember reading how Tigerpaw attacked Tiny in the super edition "Bluestar's Prophecy," and how shocking I found it. Plus I knew from years ago that Scourge is this major villain. This story basically answers the question of what would happen if a cat as smart, ambitious, and courageous as Firestar went down a much darker path – and it's even more fitting given that Scourge is Firestar's half-brother. It's always interesting to read a villain's origin story. You certainly don't agree with their actions but they are understandable. I liked that the Erin Hunter team clarified that in the author's note at the beginning. Speaking of which, while this is a graphic novel, this is still a "Warriors" title, and it has Erin Hunter's great storytelling all over it!<br /><br />Artwork: I really liked the artwork! It's certainly a different style from that used in the bonus manga chapters at the end of the super editions I've read. But it was well-drawn and drew me in (no pun intended). It also helped me to better visualize certain places I had trouble imagining from before. I will say though, had it been in the traditional book format, it probably would've been quite a bit more violent than it was. For example, when I first read Tiny's assault in "Bluestar's Prophecy," it was far more appalling and gruesome. That said, I really did like it!<br /><br />Tiny/Scourge – Since the main character has the most development, he's the only one I'm gonna go into detail with. In the beginning, you really do feel for Tiny. I definitely did. I know what it's like to be different and wishing you could be like everyone else. But Tiny unfortunately has it far worse than I ever did. His own siblings bully him, and then he suffers a brutal attack from Tigerpaw just because he was in the wrong place at the wrong time. It was also interesting to see where his spiked collar came from, and how he learns to use his small size to his advantage. While I wasn't exactly rooting for him, his progression into becoming leader of BloodClan felt gradual and therefore believable. I bizarrely am looking forward to seeing what he does later on in the series.<br /><br />Various Other Characters – While the rest of the characters featured here don't get as much development, they were good for the story. You get angry at Socks and Ruby for bullying Tiny so much, even if they are kits. So even though it is awful that Scourge turns them away later on, it's not surprising. And if you know who he becomes later on, there's this tension as you read what builds up to his turning point. Points to Thistleclaw for helping to create two villains! Anyway, it was interesting how the rogues Bone and Brick became almost like his foster brothers/lackeys. And when Scourge gets the respect he's been craving all his life, there's this bizarre sense of satisfaction given all the bullying you've had to endure with him.<br /><br />Overall: While this is a short read, and that might turn some people off, I really did like what I got and thought it was a fascinating and believable origin story for a villain the Erin Hunter team describes as the closest thing to pure evil. I dread yet also anticipate reading more about Scourge in the later books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16460599014948483170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4hRjDsf3Qw54UskAseh/950KRk4q2lu0bLXYe438JLEyk/LSr9Ve0OI7FM49C15b1kurNtW75RhNIphdZH8fqg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mtj7OIu8PwLM8o5gcXb1vo8931TFfsUhkw+Zf02FXURKX2rk454i3FabU679ldQSxHwyLDofe42ymNlZpAZmXw==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText3029119202413199245" style="display:none">Erin Hunter is the pseudonym of five people: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/132369.Kate_Cary" title="Kate Cary" rel="nofollow noopener">Kate Cary</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/220345.Cherith_Baldry" title="Cherith Baldry" rel="nofollow noopener">Cherith Baldry</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/374504.Tui_T__Sutherland" title="Tui T. Together, they write the Warriors series as well as the Seekers and Survivors series. Erin Hunter is working on a new series now called Bravelands. <br /><br />Erin Hunter is inspired by a love of cats and a fascination with the ferocity of the natural world. As well as having a great respect for nature in all its forms, Erin enjoys creating rich mythical explanations for animal behavior, shaped by her interest in astronomy and standing stones.</span>
